  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_375ba49d-7a42-4fd8-b113-18f4a4e1f77f'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer5518356914902611572">Growing up in the slums of East End London, Charlie Trumper dreams of someday running his grandfather's fruit and vegetable barrow. That day comes suddenly when his grandfather dies leaving him the floundering business.   <span id="freeText5518356914902611572" style="display:none">Growing up in the slums of East End London, Charlie Trumper dreams of someday running his grandfather's fruit and vegetable barrow. That day comes suddenly when his grandfather dies leaving him the floundering business. With the help of Becky Salmon, an enterprising young woman, Charlie sets out to make a name for himself as "The Honest Trader". But the brutal onset of World War I takes Charlie far from home and into the path of a dangerous enemy whose legacy of evil follows Charlie and his family for generations.<br /><br />Encompassing three continents and spanning over sixty years, <i>As the Crow Flies</i> brings to life a magnificent tale of one man's rise from rags to riches set against the backdrop of a changing century.</span>

<div class='communityQuestionSubTitle'>
Popular Answered Questions
</div>
<div id='communityQuestionsWithAnswers'>
<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/845002-percy-comments-that-the-king-george-v">Percy comments that the king (george V?) has a great-great-great-great grandfather who was nearly murdered by Percy&#39;s ancestor, who was then exiled. Becky later laughs as she works out who the ancestor must have been. I thus assume the ancestor was reasonably famous.
It doesn&#39;t work out, because George V&#39;s grandfather would have been Prince Albert, whose ancestry is non-famous in the UK. But who was it meant to be?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_845002'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F7201.As_the_Crow_Flies">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/845002-percy-comments-that-the-king-george-v">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/845002-percy-comments-that-the-king-george-v">See all 4 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/16823124-sara"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1370307133i/16823124._UY100_CR24,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/16823124-sara">Sara</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The book lists the graduation ceremony where this exchange happened as occurring sometime between 1918-1921, which was during the reign of George V, b<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The book lists the graduation ceremony where this exchange happened as occurring sometime between 1918-1921, which was during the reign of George V, but Percy refers to the king as "Bertie" which was a nickname for King George VI. Assuming that Archer played a little more looslely with the timeline than the nickname, it would make sense that the king's great-great-great-great-grandfather was George II. Following that logic, I think it's a safe bet that Percy's ancestor was Bonnie Prince Charlie, especially considering his Scottish roots. <br /><br />I've been mulling over this question for years, since the first time I read this book. At one point in the early 2000's I actually emailed the question to the email address listed on Jeffrey Archer's web page. An assistant replied to me with words to the effect of "I have no idea, and I'm not going to ask my boss (who is a very busy internationally best-selling author) to identify a seriously minor character in a book he wrote years ago". I don't fault him/her for that!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1069839829" />
    <a title="Luffy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7407364-luffy"><img alt="Luffy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606210775p2/7407364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1069839829?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luffy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luffy" href="/user/show/7407364-luffy">Luffy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060179144" href="/book/show/1656414.As_the_Crow_Flies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=page-turner">page-turner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=chunkster">chunkster</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=review-worth-reading">review-worth-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=superb-characterization">superb-characterization</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7407364-luffy?shelf=pretty-good">pretty-good</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1069839829" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13602071441658796583">Jeffrey Archer has proven himself many times. As The Crow Flies proves that he hit the ground running and was already a very good storyteller while young. He knows that even if he repeats himself, as long as there are enough new twists to the plot of any of his book, he'll be forgiven, and his works, enjoyed.<br/><br/> I was thoroughly entertained reading this book which has a few lulls, but which forced me to have stakes in the story at a time when I felt temporarily indifferent. After all why should I c</span>
  <span id="freeText13602071441658796583" style="display:none">Jeffrey Archer has proven himself many times. As The Crow Flies proves that he hit the ground running and was already a very good storyteller while young. He knows that even if he repeats himself, as long as there are enough new twists to the plot of any of his book, he'll be forgiven, and his works, enjoyed.<br /><br /> I was thoroughly entertained reading this book which has a few lulls, but which forced me to have stakes in the story at a time when I felt temporarily indifferent. After all why should I care if a millionaire (even self made) is risking his benefits and at worst, would be a bit poorer. No skin off MY nose! Well the author had other thoughts. He made me care.<br /><br /> I no longer think Kane And Abel is this writer's best book. That praise went to Be Careful What You Wish For...now...I'm no longer sure. This book, which I've just read, is one of the strongest 5 star books I've ever rated. The plot points, fleshed out through the way characters behave, present themselves and motivate themselves, generate inexhaustible supply of surprises. Everything is perfectly clear in the book. As The Crow Flies defies any gross accusation that can be thrown at it. It deserved to be read. It's pure entertainment, of the type that can only be offered by books and their makers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13602071441658796583" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer569607770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15595002876707864143">OH my what do I say. This book was published some 20 years ago but truly it is timeless. The joy in this novel is in the story telling -- all 600 pages of it devoted to draw you into the richness of the characters as they are woven into this saga spanning decades. Many authors have made their books long-- but end up just filling the pages with fluff....not so for archer--I relished each page and was sort of disappointed when I reached the end.<br/><br/>The character's individual parts are stories within t</span>
  <span id="freeText15595002876707864143" style="display:none">OH my what do I say. This book was published some 20 years ago but truly it is timeless. The joy in this novel is in the story telling -- all 600 pages of it devoted to draw you into the richness of the characters as they are woven into this saga spanning decades. Many authors have made their books long-- but end up just filling the pages with fluff....not so for archer--I relished each page and was sort of disappointed when I reached the end.<br /><br />The character's individual parts are stories within themselves but Archer weaves them into the overall story like the master story teller he is. You will love some and really hate others as Archer brings them to life for you.<br /><br />This is really the life story of a man named Charlie Trumper born into poverty with great dreams and the disposition to fulfil them. This book was a great read and I am a better person for reading it and sharing Charlie's pursuit of his dreams and life....</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer16332669" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6042527296929458706">I'm a sucker for Jeffrey Archer, 20th Century London and epic novels, so it's no surprise that I've read "As the Crow Flies" a dozen times. Following the life of Charlie Trumper beginning at the turn of the century, the book takes readers on a journey through both world wars, the coronation of Queen Elizabeth and the swinging 60's. While the story is about Charlie's success in retail, the core of the story revolves around his wife, his son and his fierce rivalry with the Trentham family. This is</span>
  <span id="freeText6042527296929458706" style="display:none">I'm a sucker for Jeffrey Archer, 20th Century London and epic novels, so it's no surprise that I've read "As the Crow Flies" a dozen times. Following the life of Charlie Trumper beginning at the turn of the century, the book takes readers on a journey through both world wars, the coronation of Queen Elizabeth and the swinging 60's. While the story is about Charlie's success in retail, the core of the story revolves around his wife, his son and his fierce rivalry with the Trentham family. This is a fun read with plenty of drama woven through the book.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2978804611?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/57725883-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780001046535" href="/book/show/7021937-as-the-crow-flies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57725883-rob?shelf=sagas">sagas</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2978804611" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13671926469503105457">As The Crow Flies, first published in 1990.<br/><br/>This is a saga of the rags to riches life of Charlie Trumper. Not really a rags to riches story more the industrious boy from a working class back ground with big aspirations story.<br/>The period of time is from the 1910’s to the 1960’s.<br/>To say that Charlie’s life was colourful would be an understatement, from impoverished childhood with a fruit and vegetable barrow in the East End of London to the fields of France during the WW1. Then in WW2 he became Churc</span>
  <span id="freeText13671926469503105457" style="display:none">As The Crow Flies, first published in 1990.<br /><br />This is a saga of the rags to riches life of Charlie Trumper. Not really a rags to riches story more the industrious boy from a working class back ground with big aspirations story.<br />The period of time is from the 1910’s to the 1960’s.<br />To say that Charlie’s life was colourful would be an understatement, from impoverished childhood with a fruit and vegetable barrow in the East End of London to the fields of France during the WW1. Then in WW2 he became Churchill’s go to man to keep the nation fed. Last but not least, his pride and joy ‘Trumper’s Department Store’.<br />Nothing in Charlie’s life would come easy. To succeed he will have to fight tooth and nail against a family of high social standing who is out to ruin Charlie hopes and aspiration at every turn.<br />Charlie’s life unfolds to us via all the principal characters. Each character tells the same basic story but from their pov. This sounds like it should be boring but strangely enough it wasn’t. I soon found myself becoming really invested in all Charlie’s trials and tribulations and infuriated by his enemies.<br /><br />A satisfying, entertaining read and a must for lovers of family sagas.<br /><br />A recommended 4 star read. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13671926469503105457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer438115333" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3090937784325891073">Depending on which browser I've opened to read this in (I do hate epub books and the Overdrive app that can never remember my login), I've made it to about 50% of this huge chunkster, so I'm counting this towards Mt. TBR of 2015 and the GR reading challenge. 400-500 pages is a full book in my world.<br/><br/>As far as I did get - the story begins around the latter years of WWI, and focused around a set of characters in the early years of building a financial empire starting with one store at a time - groc</span>
  <span id="freeText3090937784325891073" style="display:none">Depending on which browser I've opened to read this in (I do hate epub books and the Overdrive app that can never remember my login), I've made it to about 50% of this huge chunkster, so I'm counting this towards Mt. TBR of 2015 and the GR reading challenge. 400-500 pages is a full book in my world.<br /><br />As far as I did get - the story begins around the latter years of WWI, and focused around a set of characters in the early years of building a financial empire starting with one store at a time - grocery is the first one. Usually I'd be all over a big fat saga like this, and usually I'd love all the details of the empire building, but this one fell flat for me. The biggest problem was the never-ending flip flop back to the same events, only to be recounted to the reader in another first person narrative from another character. B.O.R.I.N.G.<br /><br />Life's too short, moving on.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4984602621061301379">This is a fairly good 200 page novel, hiding inside 600 pages. It was easy to read, but not very fulfilling. I was ready to quit on it at the halfway point, as I became tired of reading of each shop being purchased with great detail about how much it cost, and what a good deal Charlie got on each one.   <span id="freeText4984602621061301379" style="display:none">This is a fairly good 200 page novel, hiding inside 600 pages. It was easy to read, but not very fulfilling. I was ready to quit on it at the halfway point, as I became tired of reading of each shop being purchased with great detail about how much it cost, and what a good deal Charlie got on each one. I continued on, and the story improved somewhat. I never felt anything for any of the characters. They all seemed one dimensional.<br /><br />I did like the way that the story switched perspective from one character to another, filling in the blanks of the story as it did so. That made for more interesting transitions, but became predictable as the story progressed.<br /><br />On the technical side... I read the novel on my Kindle. The hand written notes scattered throughout the book were almost impossible to read. <br /><br /></span>

    <a title="Dianne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2728895-dianne"><img alt="Dianne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1252701759p2/2728895.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/174554038?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dianne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dianne" href="/user/show/2728895-dianne">Dianne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer174554038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2970120697290360837">What a fun read this was. I'd never read any Jeffrey Archer, and had the impression that he was just a mystery/thriller writer. Imagine my surprise, then, to become immersed in this atmospheric novel that begins in the early 20th century in the East End of London and ranges through the years (and the continents!) until 1970, with chapters that focus on the main characters, one by one. Charlie Trumper begins life assisting his grandfather on his fruit and vegetable barrow in the East End. As he g</span>
  <span id="freeText2970120697290360837" style="display:none">What a fun read this was. I'd never read any Jeffrey Archer, and had the impression that he was just a mystery/thriller writer. Imagine my surprise, then, to become immersed in this atmospheric novel that begins in the early 20th century in the East End of London and ranges through the years (and the continents!) until 1970, with chapters that focus on the main characters, one by one. Charlie Trumper begins life assisting his grandfather on his fruit and vegetable barrow in the East End. As he grows up, he is faced with his grandfather's death, World War I, a dashing, handsome villain called Guy Trentham, and eventually a chain of events that flows from his brief unpleasant connection with Trentham at the Battle of the Marne. Charlie returns to London after the war, reconnects with Becky, his childhood friend and eventual partner, and begins to make his way in the world, eventually building up a retail empire in Chelsea, but old family secrets keep cropping up and putting roadblocks in his path. A rollicking good read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2970120697290360837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12632389801011935546" style="display:none">This book was really good. It was a great story of one man and his entire life from the age of 0-75. <br />I loved the main character, his wife and his son.<br />There was a lot of scandal, drama, backstabbing, mystery and love.<br />It kept me wanting to know more and I had so many unanswered questions until the very end.<br />This book was recommended to me by my Nanny, my Mum and my Aunt. They all loved the book and I'm glad I can say I did too.<br /><br />There was one part in the book that I didn't see coming. I was shocked/blindsided by the information about 3/4 way through the book that left a heavy weight on my shoulders for the rest of the way through my read.<br />Most people probably won't have that effect on them from it, but I invested so much feelings into a couple of the characters that it was only obvious that at some point I would feel changed.<br /><br />I am highly recommending this book for the soul fact that it took me away to another life, another time which I feel deeply in love with.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13628371679783030122"><br/><br/>It's funny how our tastes change, I think that many years ago I would have loved this book, but now I have to admit that halfway through I found myself skimming sections of it....something I very, very rarely do.<br/>It was a good story, that of a poor east end London boy, instilled with an excellent work ethic by his Grandfather, and blessed with brains and ingenuity, who makes good despite bereavement, war, and many other trials and tribulations, including making an enemy determined to undermine an</span>
  <span id="freeText13628371679783030122" style="display:none"><br /><br />It's funny how our tastes change, I think that many years ago I would have loved this book, but now I have to admit that halfway through I found myself skimming sections of it....something I very, very rarely do.<br />It was a good story, that of a poor east end London boy, instilled with an excellent work ethic by his Grandfather, and blessed with brains and ingenuity, who makes good despite bereavement, war, and many other trials and tribulations, including making an enemy determined to undermine and ruin everything he does.<br />I did enjoy the first half of this book, and because there were some interesting characters I wanted to find out what happened to them, but at times it was all just a little too good to be true.<br />There were some surprises, but the outcome of the various problems to beset the main character and his family became just too predictable. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_467254059" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/467254059" />
    <a title="Madhavi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5857276-madhavi"><img alt="Madhavi" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madhavi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madhavi" href="/user/show/5857276-madhavi">Madhavi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer467254059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3052241553523326842">Great story, characters and style of story telling. However, the execution was appalling! So many loose ends! In a minute he changed Charlie's character from a strong family figure to someone who only cares about his company! It doesn't deal with the emotional aspect at all. And the part where Charlie tries to get from from Australia to London just goes on and on! It was almost like Archer got bored with his book and just decided to finish it quickly. Extremely disappointing!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2107228351" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2107228351" />
    <a title="Tex" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54253180-tex"><img alt="Tex" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483489871p2/54253180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2107228351?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tex" href="/user/show/54253180-tex">Tex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780340558768" href="/book/show/1656415.As_The_Crow_Flies">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54253180-tex?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2107228351" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14006415493250634649">Jeffrey Archer is a master raconteur, pure and simple, and he has turned that talent to tell the story of Charlie Trumper in "As The Crow Flies".<br/><br/>Charlie grew up in the East End of London working with his Grandpa, who was a trader on the Whitechapel Road market selling fruit and veg from his barrow. When Charlie's grandfather dies so begins Charlie's journey to own a store that sold everything under one roof - the "biggest barrow in the world"!<br/><br/>Spanning seven decades Archer takes the reader throug</span>
  <span id="freeText14006415493250634649" style="display:none">Jeffrey Archer is a master raconteur, pure and simple, and he has turned that talent to tell the story of Charlie Trumper in "As The Crow Flies".<br /><br />Charlie grew up in the East End of London working with his Grandpa, who was a trader on the Whitechapel Road market selling fruit and veg from his barrow. When Charlie's grandfather dies so begins Charlie's journey to own a store that sold everything under one roof - the "biggest barrow in the world"!<br /><br />Spanning seven decades Archer takes the reader through Charlie's ups and downs, triumphs and disasters, from the battlefields of WW1 France to cities in America and Australia; from East End streets to elegant Chelsea Terrace. A story of love, ambition, heartbreak, and revenge. <br /><br />"As The Crow Flies" is an easy book to read with Archer's writing style being free flowing and engaging. His characterisations make the reader cheer for the heroes and hiss at the villains. His twists and turns and story elements, that at times make you wonder where is he taking this tale, all make sense and come together beautifully by books end. While, I must admit, at one point I was thinking that this book was turning into a poor man's "Kane and Abel" Archer turned a corner to take the story in a completely different direction which made me wonder why I doubted his storytelling prowess in the first place.<br /><br />While not his best book "As The Crow Flies" is far from his worst and gets 3.5 Whitechapel Road fruit and veg barrows out of five. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14006415493250634649" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Pat Camalliere" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41861330-pat-camalliere"><img alt="Pat Camalliere" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1428185440p2/41861330.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3473607012?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pat Camalliere" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pat Camalliere" href="/user/show/41861330-pat-camalliere">Pat Camalliere</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3473607012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12688782760130677814">After a lapse of many years, this is the second book I’ve read by Jeffrey Archer in the past year and I must admit I wish I had more of his books on my shelf. I truly loved this one. The author breaks a lot of rules by today’s standards. His books are long, with a fair amount of stretching things out more than today’s readers prefer, unorthodox structure, switches and sometimes unclear point of view. Despite all of that, it works. I got so involved with each character that when he changed to ano</span>
  <span id="freeText12688782760130677814" style="display:none">After a lapse of many years, this is the second book I’ve read by Jeffrey Archer in the past year and I must admit I wish I had more of his books on my shelf. I truly loved this one. The author breaks a lot of rules by today’s standards. His books are long, with a fair amount of stretching things out more than today’s readers prefer, unorthodox structure, switches and sometimes unclear point of view. Despite all of that, it works. I got so involved with each character that when he changed to another I was at first angry because I didn’t want to leave that character. Twenty pages later I found the new character to be just as compelling. I couldn’t stop reading, and wished it went on another 617 pages! A little predictable now and then, but I loved the characters and story so much I didn’t care. The ending was satisfying. The book will stay on my shelf with those few specials I can’t part with, except to loan to friends—only if they’re very careful to return it! </span>
  <a data-text-id="12688782760130677814" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16338962364826130694">Will not lie, this master-stroke lost the 5th star...mostly for repeating the events with every shift in the pov. (Another reason, which I won't mention on a public forum, has to do with the fact that at every new relevation-I kept wondering, if it could have been written in a manner to increase it's surprise quotient. <br/><br/>Nevertheless, this book left me with many things I hope to carry & imbibe in myself for the years to come- 1. Charlie Trumper 2. His hardworking nature & discipline is what I was </span>
  <span id="freeText16338962364826130694" style="display:none">Will not lie, this master-stroke lost the 5th star...mostly for repeating the events with every shift in the pov. (Another reason, which I won't mention on a public forum, has to do with the fact that at every new relevation-I kept wondering, if it could have been written in a manner to increase it's surprise quotient. <br /><br />Nevertheless, this book left me with many things I hope to carry &amp; imbibe in myself for the years to come- 1. Charlie Trumper 2. His hardworking nature &amp; discipline is what I was awed by faar more than his drive/ambition 3. The importance of being good &amp; doing the right thing- that oil painting incident, how it could have ended v/s how it really panned out in the end....it reminded me-HOW important it was to be perceived as a good &amp; truthful man by others. I believe that is what saved him.<br />4. Bad actions have a way of catching upto you..in this life itself &amp; also bears the the capacity to taint the life of their child as well<br /><br />This book is pure and scandalous, both at the same time! Story is 100/ but writing, particularly, the 600+p. could have been avoided.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer795843026911876580">I picked up this book expecting to get a flavor of first and second world war history amidst some Archerian fiction (somewhat similar to the Ken Follet century trilogy); however I wasn't much impressed with the history aspect of this book as much as it still kept me engrossed in the fiction. That being said I would consider this book to be a soap opera entertainer of fiction; I wouldn't consider it to be the best in terms of historical fiction; I would still consider it to be an entertaining bea</span>
  <span id="freeText795843026911876580" style="display:none">I picked up this book expecting to get a flavor of first and second world war history amidst some Archerian fiction (somewhat similar to the Ken Follet century trilogy); however I wasn't much impressed with the history aspect of this book as much as it still kept me engrossed in the fiction. That being said I would consider this book to be a soap opera entertainer of fiction; I wouldn't consider it to be the best in terms of historical fiction; I would still consider it to be an entertaining beach read. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('j21+VjKovCFC8ku2y7FDWRWOd7OmCWEqLmN5rsTPV4O3gjiKPm2vj2MGXb79je/wZ99ovQ3A4WfepxxJLSmxTg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ri0r7b6OxkEThoAV0accusL2T0ZWn6L3GSXpE+jc/BOWwm0xskvV7zJylh3nm7ATsKdQSP1WIrrp4Yz0AToa3g==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4820.Jeffrey_Archer">About Jeffrey Archer</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/4820.Jeffrey_Archer"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1208462800p3/4820.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16672599165197707500">Jeffrey Howard Archer, Baron Archer of Weston-super-Mare (born 15 April 1940) is an English author and former politician.<br/><br/>He was a Member of Parliament and deputy chairman of the Conservative Party, and became a life peer in 1992. His political career, having suffered several controversies, ended after a conviction for perverting the course of justice and his subsequent imprisonment. He is married </span>
  <span id="freeText16672599165197707500" style="display:none">Jeffrey Howard Archer, Baron Archer of Weston-super-Mare (born 15 April 1940) is an English author and former politician.<br /><br />He was a Member of Parliament and deputy chairman of the Conservative Party, and became a life peer in 1992. His political career, having suffered several controversies, ended after a conviction for perverting the course of justice and his subsequent imprisonment. He is married to Mary Archer, a scientist specialising in solar power. Outside politics, he is a novelist, playwright and short story writer.<br /><br /><a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeffrey_Archer" rel="nofollow noopener">Wikipedia link</a><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/jeffreyarcher">http://us.macmillan.com/author/jeffre...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16672599165197707500" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
